  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_bf1d4fd4-46a2-46a9-95da-34025616666e'
      });
    }

  <span id="freeText2937411309479456571" style="display:none"><strong>From Shel Silverstein, the celebrated author of <em>The Giving Tree</em> and <em>Where the Sidewalk Ends</em>, comes <em>The Missing Piece</em>, a charming fable that gently probes the nature of quest and fulfillment.</strong><br /><br /><em>It was missing a piece. And it was not happy. </em>What it finds on its search for the missing piece is simply and touchingly told. This inventive and heartwarming book can be read on many levels, and Silverstein’s iconic drawings and humor are sure to delight fans of all ages.<br /><br /><em>So it set off in search<br />of its missing piece.<br />And as it rolled<br />it sang this song— <br />Oh I'm lookin' for my missin' piece<br />I'm lookin' for my missin' piece<br />Hi-dee-ho, here I go,<br />Lookin' for my missin' piece.</em><br /><br />And don't miss <em>Runny Babbit Returns</em>, the new book from Shel Silverstein!</span>

<div id="review_124399084" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/124399084" />
    <a title="Jason Koivu" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1742824-jason-koivu"><img alt="Jason Koivu" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560521450p2/1742824.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/124399084?book_show_action=true">Oct 02, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jason Koivu" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jason Koivu" href="/user/show/1742824-jason-koivu">Jason Koivu</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer124399084" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12223424788555486764">A brilliant, edge-of-your-seat masterpiece! Dynamic character development and a knock-your-socks-off climatic twist! I couldn't get enough of <i>The Missing Piece</i> when I was eight years old! However, that Shel Silverstein is a one creepy looking dude. There's a certain sort of child molester-esque look about him. His picture on the jacket sleeve alone could deter readers and nearly made me drop the rating down a half star, but I wear big boy pants now and the Silverstein booger monsters of the worl</span>
  <span id="freeText12223424788555486764" style="display:none">A brilliant, edge-of-your-seat masterpiece! Dynamic character development and a knock-your-socks-off climatic twist! I couldn't get enough of <i>The Missing Piece</i> when I was eight years old! However, that Shel Silverstein is a one creepy looking dude. There's a certain sort of child molester-esque look about him. His picture on the jacket sleeve alone could deter readers and nearly made me drop the rating down a half star, but I wear big boy pants now and the Silverstein booger monsters of the world no longer bias my reviews!<br /><br />This is the perfect parable for relationships. This guy roams about looking for his missing piece (hello!), trying different ones on for size and not finding the right fit. Sometimes the fit is too loose and sometimes he holds on too tight. Even if he finds a match, that particular piece does want to feel owned by another. So on he rolls, having adventures, living life and enjoying the ride. And then one day he does find that perfect piece, the one that's been missing all his life and everything seems great! He and his piece are flying high. But then he realizes life is passing him by too fast and he can't sing his song anymore. He is stifled. He's missing out on life. He lets his piece go. He goes on singing his song, enjoying life. <br /><br />Part of me thinks: Good for him!<br /><br />Part of me thinks, sure, he wants to roam free, okay, but he leaves the perfect piece in the lurch: What a dick!</span>
  <a data-text-id="12223424788555486764" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_666534202" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/666534202" />
    <a title="Matthew Hunter" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3040804-matthew-hunter"><img alt="Matthew Hunter" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1495642903p2/3040804.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/666534202?book_show_action=true">Jul 13, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matthew Hunter" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matthew Hunter" href="/user/show/3040804-matthew-hunter">Matthew Hunter</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3040804-matthew-hunter?shelf=children-picture-books">children-picture-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer666534202" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12539625869357452299">I can see why many consider <i>The Missing Piece</i> to promote individualism over relationship. But there's more to the story here. It's not so much that Silverstein's telling us to avoid relationships like the plague, he's cautioning us not to seek completion in other people, ideas, or things. Relationships are hard anyway, and when we approach them from a needy place, we might hold on to them so tightly that the break from the pressure of being another's all-in-all. Or we might get distracted by our</span>
  <span id="freeText12539625869357452299" style="display:none">I can see why many consider <i>The Missing Piece</i> to promote individualism over relationship. But there's more to the story here. It's not so much that Silverstein's telling us to avoid relationships like the plague, he's cautioning us not to seek completion in other people, ideas, or things. Relationships are hard anyway, and when we approach them from a needy place, we might hold on to them so tightly that the break from the pressure of being another's all-in-all. Or we might get distracted by our own pain, take them for granted, and let them slip away.<br /><br />And Silverstein's not just talking about relationships here. He's talking about our life journeys. No ideology, wealth level, or achievement will make us complete. We don't journey toward completeness or perfection in our lifetimes. Such grasping at completeness makes us miserable, takes the song out of our lives. We muddle our identity, confuse our sense of selves with other people or material accumulations. Of course, I could be wrong.<br /><br />Oh yeah, Sigourney requested multiple reads of this one. She absolutely loved the Pac Man-like main character and the simple black and white line drawings. And yet another plus--it's the first picture book I've encountered where I'm talented enough to have been the illustrator.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12539625869357452299" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_783509069" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/783509069" />
    <a title="Ronyell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1169488-ronyell"><img alt="Ronyell" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1506581787p2/1169488.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/783509069?book_show_action=true">Dec 07, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ronyell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ronyell" href="/user/show/1169488-ronyell">Ronyell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=picture-book">picture-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=read-in-2013">read-in-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=shel-silverstein">shel-silverstein</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=my-blog-reviews">my-blog-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=children-s-book">children-s-book</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer783509069" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5534566633020428777"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1386418151i/7360199.jpg' width='400' height='300' alt='Missing' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Even to this very day, I am still reading Shel Silverstein’s works and I am finding them much more interesting than ever before! Now, I have recently picked up another book by Shel Silverstein called “The Missing Piece” and man, was this one enjoyable read!<br/><br/>Basically, this book is about a circle who is missing a piece of itself and how it tries to find its missing piece through snowy weather and through mountains. While on the way, the circle meets up with several triangular shaped pieces that th</span>
  <span id="freeText5534566633020428777" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1386418151i/7360199.jpg" width="400" height="300" alt="Missing" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Even to this very day, I am still reading Shel Silverstein’s works and I am finding them much more interesting than ever before! Now, I have recently picked up another book by Shel Silverstein called “The Missing Piece” and man, was this one enjoyable read!<br><br>Basically, this book is about a circle who is missing a piece of itself and how it tries to find its missing piece through snowy weather and through mountains. While on the way, the circle meets up with several triangular shaped pieces that the circle tries on itself, but none of the triangular pieces would fit the circle.<br><br>Shel Silverstein has done it again in providing us a book that tries to give out a lesson in life, just like his well-known and controversial book, “The Giving Tree.” I loved the fact that this story tackles the issue about people going on personal journeys to find their true purpose in life and in this case, the circle was trying to find its missing piece to make itself complete. That is a truly insightful way to state the theme of people trying to find their goals in life and I am sure that children will easily understand the message of this book, even if it is told in a completely simplified way. I also loved the little song that the circle sings as it goes on its journey to find its missing piece which goes something like this:<br><br><b>
  <i>“Oh I’m lookin’ for my missin’ piece<br>I’m lookin’ for my missin’ piece<br>Hi-dee-ho, here I go,<br>Lookin’ for my missin’ piece.”</i>
</b><br><br>Shel Silverstein’s illustrations are cute and simple and I enjoyed seeing the images of the circle crossing across various landscapes to get to his destination such as rolling up a mountain, going through a swamp and trudging through a snow storm.<br><br>Overall, “The Missing Piece” is a truly memorable and inspiring tale about understanding your goals in life and pursuing them whenever you desire to and children will easily enjoy this tale for many years! I would recommend this book to children ages three and up since there is nothing inappropriate in this book.<br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1385664778i/7198025._SX540_.jpg" width="200" height="100" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Review is also on: <a href="http://rabbitearsbookblog.blogspot.com/2013/12/the-missing-piece-by-shel-silverstein.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Rabbit Ears Book Blog</a></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="5534566633020428777" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2347078067" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2347078067" />
    <a title="Josh Caporale" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5687551-josh-caporale"><img alt="Josh Caporale" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1431172307p2/5687551.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2347078067?book_show_action=true">Jul 20, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Josh Caporale" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Josh Caporale" href="/user/show/5687551-josh-caporale">Josh Caporale</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2347078067" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12638213096526570461">The Missing Piece was quite a delight. It is a great exploration within the simplicity, but yet the great depth of what Shel Silverstein has to offer when it comes to basic wisdom for young readers. In this case, a Pac-Man-like character is looking for a "missing piece" in order to seek a sense of completion, but it realizes that one does not necessarily need a particular attribute or object in order to seek perfection and that perfection is something that comes from within. I can definitely see</span>
  <span id="freeText12638213096526570461" style="display:none">The Missing Piece was quite a delight. It is a great exploration within the simplicity, but yet the great depth of what Shel Silverstein has to offer when it comes to basic wisdom for young readers. In this case, a Pac-Man-like character is looking for a "missing piece" in order to seek a sense of completion, but it realizes that one does not necessarily need a particular attribute or object in order to seek perfection and that perfection is something that comes from within. I can definitely see where the book is a bit too simple and how the ending is so open-ended, but its underlying message definitely hits home and this was an enjoyable read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12638213096526570461" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1360014443" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13908304429098995757">Growing up I remember Shel Silverstein's books distinctly because I have never seen those types of illustrations in the front cover and even though I was too little to read them I was fascinated at looking at the pictures. Then going a few years back I read some recommendations of pictures book that will impact your life and this book was included in the list. I only remember now to read it after I recently read <i>The Giving Tree</i> and found that the library has this book. <br/><br/>Even though the story did </span>
  <span id="freeText13908304429098995757" style="display:none">Growing up I remember Shel Silverstein's books distinctly because I have never seen those types of illustrations in the front cover and even though I was too little to read them I was fascinated at looking at the pictures. Then going a few years back I read some recommendations of pictures book that will impact your life and this book was included in the list. I only remember now to read it after I recently read <i>The Giving Tree</i> and found that the library has this book. <br /><br />Even though the story did not impact me I still love the story, the simple illustrations, and the humor of this book. It deals with a circle who is missing a piece of himself so he practically looks like Pac-Man. He gets sad and gloomy about the situation and decides to go on a journey in pursuits of finding the missing piece. <br /><br />What I loved about this book is that in a way in reflects how sometimes the hunt is greater than the catch. We as human beings are constantly in a journey towards reaching our goals whether it be physical, spiritual, or emotional and we get so caught up on trying to reach the top of the mountain that we forget and enjoy the experience of the journey. I believe this book even though it is a children's book is dedicated more to adults cause I know if I was a kid and someone read me this story I wouldn't understand the circle and why he did what he did in the end. It was a quick short read but I enjoyed it nonetheless and I found out that it has a sequel so I placed an order now at the library and hopefully get to read it asap.<br /><br /><i>P.S. If you want to check out the sequel the link is here. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/525958.The_Missing_Piece_Meets_the_Big_O" title="The Missing Piece Meets the Big O by Shel Silverstein" rel="nofollow noopener">The Missing Piece Meets the Big O</a></i></span>
  <a data-text-id="13908304429098995757" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer3558334428188721874">I love <i>The Missing Piece</i>. What youngsters will see as a fantasy story about a Pacman-like creature (identified only as "It") who is searching for its missing piece, adults will identify as a book about the trajectory of relationships. <br/><br/>Older readers may get a bit misty when "it" finds a piece but doesn't hold on tightly enough, so it slips away--only to have the next piece break when it clings to it too tightly. <br/><br/>Finally, it discovers a piece that fits just right, but they become so entangled in e</span>
  <span id="freeText3558334428188721874" style="display:none">I love <i>The Missing Piece</i>. What youngsters will see as a fantasy story about a Pacman-like creature (identified only as "It") who is searching for its missing piece, adults will identify as a book about the trajectory of relationships. <br /><br />Older readers may get a bit misty when "it" finds a piece but doesn't hold on tightly enough, so it slips away--only to have the next piece break when it clings to it too tightly. <br /><br />Finally, it discovers a piece that fits just right, but they become so entangled in each other that it no longer does all of the things it used to enjoy. It loses its identity. It also loses the piece, and rolls off happily, once again singing about finding its missing piece. The moral is that relationships can never live up to our expectations, and the fun and joy may be in searching for "The One," rather than actually locating him/her. <br /><br />I think it's funny that this book is sometimes given as a wedding gift, because in actuality it is quite anti-relationship. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3558334428188721874" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_99648170" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/99648170" />
    <a title="Victoria" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3623530-victoria"><img alt="Victoria" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483509717p2/3623530.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/99648170?book_show_action=true">Apr 22, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Victoria" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Victoria" href="/user/show/3623530-victoria">Victoria</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer99648170" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8039118818418881172">This is one of the most amazing books I have ever read in my life. Silverstein is a genius at metaphor. About a year after my separation from my husband, I was going through some boxes and I came across this book. I had written the date on it that the book club had sent it to my son. I had taped a picture of my son (at the age he was when he received the book... about 4 years old). <br/><br/>I pushed the box aside and read the book. I realized that everything was going to be ok. I was the "piece". Somethi</span>
  <span id="freeText8039118818418881172" style="display:none">This is one of the most amazing books I have ever read in my life. Silverstein is a genius at metaphor. About a year after my separation from my husband, I was going through some boxes and I came across this book. I had written the date on it that the book club had sent it to my son. I had taped a picture of my son (at the age he was when he received the book... about 4 years old). <br /><br />I pushed the box aside and read the book. I realized that everything was going to be ok. I was the "piece". Something was missing right then, but there was no guarantee that finding something to fit in the hole would fix anything at all. I cried and I still keep that book on my bookshelf in my front room, even though it's a children's book and my children are much past the age of that book. Loved it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8039118818418881172" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          </span>

<div id="review_191897838" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/191897838" />
    <a title="Sarah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4549009-sarah"><img alt="Sarah" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/191897838?book_show_action=true">Jul 29, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah" href="/user/show/4549009-sarah">Sarah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer191897838" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15185685115083250387">"Hi," it said.<br/>"Hi," said the piece.<br/>"Are you anybody else's missing piece?"<br/>"Not that I know of."<br/>"Well, maybe you want to be your own piece?"<br/>"I can be someone's and still be my own."<br/>"Well, maybe you don't want to be mine."<br/>"Maybe I do."<br/>"Maybe we won't fit...."<br/>"Well..."<br/>"Hummm?"<br/>"Ummmm!"<br/>It fit!<br/>It fit perfectly!<br/>At last! At last!<br/>And away it rolled<br/>and because it was now complete,<br/>it rolled faster and faster. <br/>Faster than it had ever rolled before!<br/>So fast that it could not stop to talk to a worm<br/>or smell a f</span>
  <span id="freeText15185685115083250387" style="display:none">"Hi," it said.<br />"Hi," said the piece.<br />"Are you anybody else's missing piece?"<br />"Not that I know of."<br />"Well, maybe you want to be your own piece?"<br />"I can be someone's and still be my own."<br />"Well, maybe you don't want to be mine."<br />"Maybe I do."<br />"Maybe we won't fit...."<br />"Well..."<br />"Hummm?"<br />"Ummmm!"<br />It fit!<br />It fit perfectly!<br />At last! At last!<br />And away it rolled<br />and because it was now complete,<br />it rolled faster and faster. <br />Faster than it had ever rolled before!<br />So fast that it could not stop to talk to a worm<br />or smell a flower<br />Too fast for a butterfly to land.<br />But it could sing its happy song, at last it could sing "I've found my missing piece."<br />And it began to sing-<br /> "I've frown my nizzin' geez, uf vroun my mitzin' brees<br /> so krease ny meas an bleez ny drees uf frown..."<br />Oh my, now that it was complete it could not sing at all.<br />"Aha," it thought. "So that's how it is!"<br />So it stopped rolling...<br />And it set the piece down gently, and slowly rolled away<br />and as it rolled it softly sang - <br />"Oh I'm lookin' for my missin' piece, I'm lookin' for my missin' piece<br />Hi-dee-ho, here I go, lookin' for my missin' piece."</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('TmLCcwfjZ67hkNYH+yMSnQsE2Jq4gp4nw/c8PrKT7noT6w1OT+EskfvA/i7yDm8d1QZCpqIH5pjPnYHm4H68qA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('qV8sfhLvSmmQqHO+Iz+JWzG8vcUPwBGvW8lTXYS00E/01uNDWu0BVor4W5cqEvTb774n+RVFaRBXo+6F1lmCnQ==')})
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer17381661049616905673">Shel Silverstein was the author-artist of many beloved books of prose and poetry. He was a cartoonist, playwright, poet, performer, recording artist, and Grammy-winning, Oscar-nominated songwriter.</span>
